  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_79b5f1b8-e145-45f3-8225-edb534121558'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };
    if (typeof AppleID !== "undefined") {
      initAppleId();
    } else {
      initializeSiwa();
    }

<span id="freeTextContainer11027104065138273670">Way too young, eleven year old Tucker Creed and his six year old neighbor, Sylvie Bissenette, find they have something awful in common. Creed then decides he’s going to do everything in his limited power to shield his Sylvie from her ordeal.   <span id="freeText11027104065138273670" style="display:none">Way too young, eleven year old Tucker Creed and his six year old neighbor, Sylvie Bissenette, find they have something awful in common. Creed then decides he’s going to do everything in his limited power to shield his Sylvie from her ordeal. So he does and Creed and Sylvie form a bond that grows and blossoms with their ages.<br /><br />They plot to leave their lives behind, the town they live in that will hold them down and the histories they share that, unless they break free, will bury them. Sylvie goes to their special place, Creed never shows and she doesn’t see him again until it’s too late.<br /><br />With Creed gone, Sylvie is forced to endure a nightmare and do the unspeakable to end it. To deal, she develops a hard shell with sharp edges that very few can break through. So when Creed again finds his Sylvie, he discovers the girl he loved is locked away and he has to find his way back into her heart without getting shredded in the process.</span>
  <a data-text-id="11027104065138273670" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_392528347" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/392528347" />
    <a title="Kristen" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5477946-kristen"><img alt="Kristen" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1312922334p2/5477946.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/392528347?book_show_action=true">Aug 15, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kristen" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kristen" href="/user/show/5477946-kristen">Kristen</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5477946-kristen?shelf=anti-hero">anti-hero</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5477946-kristen?shelf=bittersweet-plot">bittersweet-plot</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5477946-kristen?shelf=loved-the-love-story">loved-the-love-story</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5477946-kristen?shelf=exhausting-read">exhausting-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5477946-kristen?shelf=outstanding-epilogue">outstanding-epilogue</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5477946-kristen?shelf=strong-willed-heroine">strong-willed-heroine</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5477946-kristen?shelf=fabulous-characters">fabulous-characters</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5477946-kristen?shelf=fabulous-hero">fabulous-hero</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5477946-kristen?shelf=fabulous-heroine">fabulous-heroine</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5477946-kristen?shelf=heartbreaking">heartbreaking</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer392528347" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15315848776413846085"><b>
  <u>5 STARS</u>
</b><br/><br/>Wow! Just wow! What a ride, bumps and all. Simply fantastic! I ended up loving this book. Not because it's my favorite Kristen Ashely story, it's not, but because of it's gritty, and raw, and authentic feel. <br/><br/>Sylvie and Creed, two characters I adore, breathe life into every page of this story. It's obvious from the beginning that this is their story—and Kristen Ashley their storyteller. Their heartbreaking yet triumphant love story had me feeling a kaleidoscope of emotions on every pag</span>
  <span id="freeText15315848776413846085" style="display:none"><b>
  <u>5 STARS</u>
</b><br><br>Wow! Just wow! What a ride, bumps and all. Simply fantastic! I ended up loving this book. Not because it's my favorite Kristen Ashely story, it's not, but because of it's gritty, and raw, and authentic feel. <br><br>Sylvie and Creed, two characters I adore, breathe life into every page of this story. It's obvious from the beginning that this is their story—and Kristen Ashley their storyteller. Their heartbreaking yet triumphant love story had me feeling a kaleidoscope of emotions on every page. I felt anger, betrayal, devastation, horror, frustration, humor, happiness, elation, giddiness, hopefulness, tenderness, and overwhelming love. It was simply magnificent! <br><br>The epilogue was beautiful, touching, emotional, and exactly what these two soul mates, and I, yearned for and wholeheartedly deserved. I've never felt such happiness or joy as I did while reading Creed and Sylvie's much deserved, and, frankly, earned ending.<br><br>A book that has the power to elicit such strong emotions and reactions from me, regardless of my misgivings, deserves a five star rating. <br><br>Slight spoiler. Please  read with caution. <br><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Like a few of you, I struggled with Creed's choice not to check up on Sylvie through the years. To make sure her "daddy" kept his promise and to personally know, for himself, she was okay and happy. That said, and after reading the book, finding out all that happened to him; what he was lead to believe; and the choice he made to protect her; I do not feel Creed could have dealt with checking up on Sylvie throughout the years. He handled what happened to him the only way he knew how, and did what he could to personally (tattoo, kids names, the necklaces) keep her close to him through the years. Was it the right decision? No. Was it a human response?  Most definitely! <br><br>Not to mention, Sylvie would have never have taken him back had she not understood his views, what he was lead to believe, and how that affected him throughout the years. She even explains this to Charlene during a segment of the book:<br><br><i>"So I helped her get the rest of the way. "There's no one but him. No one. I want our future, the one that was stolen from us. I want it for me and I <i>needed</i> to give it to him. He was..." I hesitated, having shared a bit but not entirely and deciding not to, for Creed. "I can't say, what I can say is that I explained it all came out and we worked it out. What you can guess is, we're together so the reason he disappeared was understandable. So understandable, there's not even anything to forgive."</i><br><br>Still, I plan to ask Kristen Ashley her thoughts and feelings on this matter. I want to know if my assumptions are correct.  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br>I know this book was not a hit with everyone, but for me, Creed, is one of Kristen Ashley's better works. I feel it's her most authentic book to-date, and I simply loved it.<br><br>Song Note: <i>Where The River Goes</i>, by  Zac Brown Band, captures the overall ambiance of this book for me. There is a haunting feel to this song that reminds me of Creed and his Sylvie. <br><br><a href="http://s571.photobucket.com/albums/ss158/kpeery1/KA%20Group/?action=view&amp;current=3542A2FA-DB5D-4214-BC08-2DE18D3E49AC-234-00000017BF03DDE5-1.jpg" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380387775i/747985.jpg" alt="Photobucket Pictures, Images and Photos" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.youtube.com/watch?v=5xzdcG955KQ&amp;feature=youtube_gdata_player">http://www.youtube.com/watch?v=5xzdcG...</a><br><br><b><u>September 19, 2012 Update</u>: For those of you who expressed an interest in Kristen Ashley's response to the reason Creed never checked up on Sylvie through the years, here is the link to her answer. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/topic/show/978926?page=1&amp;utm_content=A&amp;utm_medium=email&amp;utm_source=comment_instant" rel="nofollow noopener"> Questions For Kristen-Message 40</a> </b><br><br><i>If you're already a Kristen Ashley addict, or interested in checking out her books, be sure to stop by our <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/group/show/66492.Kristen_Ashley_Addict_s_Support_Group" rel="nofollow noopener">Kristen Ashley Addict's Support Group</a> here on Goodreads!</i></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer14767157336200111509"><br/><b>May 4th, 2013<br/><br/>Pre-reveal of the paperback cover for CREED!</b><br/><br/><a href='http://s385.photobucket.com/user/ohbleep/media/Book%20Stuff/CreedNewCover_zps4017befd.jpeg.html' target='_blank' rel='nofollow noopener'>

</a><br/><br/> <br/>Review:<br/><br/>I spent literally hours a day, for a few days, trying to write a review for this book and all I got, time after time, was a bunch of raving and gushing and corny rambling so I’ll just break it down this way because it reminds me of Creed and Sylvie's innocence and their naïvete of adolescence and first love, and then all the deeper, more compelling things that make up their relationship as adults.<b>
  <blockquote>
    <blockquote>
      <blockquote>C - Complex<br/>R - R</blockquote></blockquote></blockquote></b></span>
  <span id="freeText14767157336200111509" style="display:none"><br><b>May 4th, 2013<br><br>Pre-reveal of the paperback cover for CREED!</b><br><br><a href="http://s385.photobucket.com/user/ohbleep/media/Book%20Stuff/CreedNewCover_zps4017befd.jpeg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1379791140i/546515.jpg" alt="Creed New Cover photo CreedNewCover_zps4017befd.jpeg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br> <br>Review:<br><br>I spent literally hours a day, for a few days, trying to write a review for this book and all I got, time after time, was a bunch of raving and gushing and corny rambling so I’ll just break it down this way because it reminds me of Creed and Sylvie's innocence and their naïvete of adolescence and first love, and then all the deeper, more compelling things that make up their relationship as adults.<b>
  <blockquote>
    <blockquote>
      <blockquote>C - Complex<br>R - Raw<br>E - Edgy<br>E - Exciting<br>D - Devoted<blockquote><b>+</b></blockquote>S - Sexy<br>Y - Yearning<br>L - Loving<br>V - Vital<br>I - Intelligent<br>E - Enigmatic<blockquote><b>=</b></blockquote>P - Passionate<br>E - Enduring<br>R - Romantic<br>F - Fevered<br>E - Erotic<br>C - Complete<br>T - Triumphant</blockquote>
    </blockquote>
  </blockquote>
</b>And this is why <i>Creed, </i> the second book in the <i>Unfinished Hero</i> series, might just be my favorite Kristen Ashley story, ever! Amazing, solid, sexy, romantic, poignant, heartbreaking, uplifting… <i>Creed</i> is all those things and so much more, and precisely the reason Kristen Ashley is quickly becoming the Queen Diva of Storytelling, regardless of the genre she writes!<br><br>------------------<br><br>If you're already a Kristen Ashley addict, or interested in checking out her books, be sure to stop by our <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/group/show/66492.Kristen_Ashley_Addict_s_Support_Group" rel="nofollow noopener">Kristen Ashley Addict's Support Group</a> here on Goodreads!</span>

<div id="review_358715926" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/358715926" />
    <a title="Baba  " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4669232-baba"><img alt="Baba  " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1564910043p2/4669232.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/358715926?book_show_action=true">Jun 30, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Baba  " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Baba  " href="/user/show/4669232-baba">Baba  </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer358715926" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11499746076670133471"><b>Review edited September 18, 2012,</b> <i>(new paragraph in italic)</i><br/><br/><b>DNF when I hit the 70 % mark.<br/><br/>On a personal note</b><br/><i>Honesty is the best policy.</i><br/><br/>Kit, I am very sorry. I really tried very hard to like your book and its characters. Well, you win some and you lose some and unfortunately it was a lost cause. And I know that reading a book is a very personal experience and everyone's opinion is bound to be subjective. Kit, I adore your work and I believe that you are a fantastic storyteller. Having said that, it</span>
  <span id="freeText11499746076670133471" style="display:none"><b>Review edited September 18, 2012,</b> <i>(new paragraph in italic)</i><br><br><b>DNF when I hit the 70 % mark.<br><br>On a personal note</b><br><i>Honesty is the best policy.</i><br><br>Kit, I am very sorry. I really tried very hard to like your book and its characters. Well, you win some and you lose some and unfortunately it was a lost cause. And I know that reading a book is a very personal experience and everyone's opinion is bound to be subjective. Kit, I adore your work and I believe that you are a fantastic storyteller. Having said that, it really saddens me to admit that Creed did not work for me at all. After loving <i>Knight</i> I just expected way more but as a matter of fact, Creed couldn't live up to my high expectations.<br><br>***************<br><br>Where Creed most certainly failed for me...<br><br>The sex<br>The heroine<br>The plot<br>The repetitiveness in characterization, speech, behavior and plot<br><br><i>Creed</i> is supposed to be an erotic romance book. I think that the blurb was kinda misleading. What was kinky about Creed? Nothing at all. Further, a great erotic story provides great erotic, steamy and HOT sex scenes. The sex in Creed was neither hot nor erotic. It was boring and repetitive. Sure, there were some varying positions, but first and foremost the sex felt too mechanic and detached. I don't necessarily need to read how many times a hero/heroine could orgasm. Sometimes less is more. What I mean is I want a hot AND explicit sex scene that is well developed. A scene that provides CHEMISTRY as all get out. Instead of writing three short ones, write one that will make me want to combust. As a reader I can't push a specific button and all of my girlie parts will feel hot and bothered. I need a certain build-up. I want sexual tension and please…I want sensuality.<br><br>I love heroines who kick ass. Sadly, I really disliked Sylvie--she was just OTT. I have read so many KA books and I don't mind when her characters are dropping the F-bomb. But Sylvie? That's not cool anymore. That's NOT badass either. A woman who is cussing all the time is simply a turn-off. The term f*ck/f*cked/f*cking etc. has been used <b>!392!</b> times. Admittedly, Sylvie is not the only perpetrator but then again, she used foul language all the time during the first half of the plot. It was too much. Period. Even though Creed was more or less all right I felt that Sylvie almost overshadowed him. Hence, it's possible that two badass MCs can't go hand in hand 'cause there's too much friction.<br><br>The plot was "meh" and some parts of Creed dragged and couldn't hold my attention. I could feel how my interest slowly yet steadily petered out. Well, I think I won't bother to go into details here. <br><br><i>Finally, I also feel there is a repetitiveness in characterization, speech, behavior and plot. I have read so many KA books by now that Creed, the character, was nothing special to me anymore. Sure, I liked him well enough but he was a common reflection of many other KA heroes. One of my friends wrote “Saturation point, maybe?” This is a valid question and it has its “raison d’être”. However, I will gladly read the next fifty KA books <b>if</b> I get a better quality. Having said that, it’s possible that cranking out so many books in such a short time span won’t help to improve the quality of the stories though. Maybe it’s time to reconsider and the benefit of taking a little bit more time to develop a plot and its characters ought to translate into both better quality and maybe less stress for the author. It could be very favorable on so many levels. Hearing or reading criticism is not pleasant, I completely understand that. But I try to give a constructive feedback and I believe that if you don’t go forward, you go backwards. </i><br><br>Overall Creed was a disappointment. In fact, I'm reading a book for my personal pleasure, and if I can't enjoy a story and their characters then it's better to move on. <br><br><br><br>*********************************<br><br><b>My preliminary thoughts after having read the working chapters:</b><br><br><b>Mid-September can't come soon enough!! The thrill of anticipation...</b><br><br><a href="http://s1071.beta.photobucket.com/user/MsBaba4/media/FUN/MEN-AND-MEN-WOMEN/Bildschirmfoto2012-12-26um232041_zps00050c50.png.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380351936i/705487._SX540_.png" alt="Photobucket" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>So far I really like Sylvie. She's got a gun, she kicks ass and she drives a Corvette. She can hold her own, that's for sure, and there's no damsel in distress to be seen…at the moment. :-)<br><br>Love me some <b>
  <i>Creed.</i>
</b> From the cutest boy in town to a hard-edged and scarred man who features a beautiful smile.<br><br>Boy, these two are bitching at one another...<br><br><i>“God granted me peripheral vision, Creed. I can see someone coming. I’ll slow and roll through like normal. You’ll be fine.”<br>“Jesus, Sylvie, the slow and roll doesn’t work. A stop sign is put up for a reason.”<br>I cocked my head to the side and narrowed my eyes. “When did you get a stick planted up your ass?”<br>He cocked his head to the side and regarded me closely. “We talkin’ about our pasts now?”<br>F*ck, f*ck, f*ck!<br>“Okay, I’ll stop at stop signs,” I gave in.</i><br><br><a href="http://s1071.photobucket.com/albums/u520/MsBaba4/kissing/?action=view&amp;current=tumblr_m7sm11b4j51rz9boio1_500.gif" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380222758ra/346052.gif" alt="Photobucket" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br></span>
  <a data-text-id="11499746076670133471" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5604583-aestas-book-blog?shelf=6-star-books">6-star-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5604583-aestas-book-blog?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer422075849" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2352137879792668110"><img width='100%' src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380392403i/755399._SY540_.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><b> 5++ stars!!! (maybe even 6) </b><br/><br/>I seriously <i> <b> LOVED </b></i>  this book!!! I loved Sylvie. I loved Creed. Their story broke my heart and despite adoring it, emotionally, it ripped my heart out. It was a heart wrenching, tragic, BEAUTIFUL love story about survival of loss...<br/><br/>But you know, the most tragic stories of loss make for some of the most heart warming and MEANINGFUL reunions -every moment of good becomes unimaginably precious. Full. Earned. Treasured…. that what this story is about.<br/><br/><blockquote> <b> <i> “I’m not what y</i></b></blockquote></span>
  <span id="freeText2352137879792668110" style="display:none"><img width="100%" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380392403i/755399._SY540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b> 5++ stars!!! (maybe even 6) </b><br><br>I seriously <i> <b> LOVED </b></i>  this book!!! I loved Sylvie. I loved Creed. Their story broke my heart and despite adoring it, emotionally, it ripped my heart out. It was a heart wrenching, tragic, BEAUTIFUL love story about survival of loss...<br><br>But you know, the most tragic stories of loss make for some of the most heart warming and MEANINGFUL reunions -every moment of good becomes unimaginably precious. Full. Earned. Treasured…. that what this story is about.<br><br><blockquote> <b> <i> “I’m not what you want, Sylvie, I get that because its the same for you as it is for me. I’m not what you want ’cause I’m what you </i> need.” </b> </blockquote><br><br>When Sylvie was six and Creed was eleven, they met in the woods one night – both trying to get away from the misery wrapped up in their homes. Over the years, their bond is forged and cemented – they helped each other, sheltered each other, supported each other, fell in love, made plans to get away. But on the night they were supposed to leave, Creed never showed. He just disappeared….. Cut to present day, sixteen years later, Sylvie is working for Knight’s business in the security department. When there is a breach, he calls in Creed – not knowing of their connection. Suddenly faced with the man who abandoned her so many years ago and forced into a situation where they have to partner up for a job, Sylvie has no choice but to deal with the past she’s been trying to put behind her… But it all leads to one very important question: Why did he abandon her? What could have happened to make him never show up?<br><br>Let me tell you , I was feeling really betrayed and hurt by him at that point. All I could think about was how on earth could he abandon her after everything they’d been through together and promised each other, and not communicate for sixteen years… I couldn’t think of a single reason that would honestly justify that. I went through a period of extreme HURT and betrayal while I was reading. My heart ached. It was a physical pain. I felt ill. It was the strongest hurt I’ve EVER felt from any of KA’s character’s actions.<br><br>I was desperately wracking my brain to come up with ANY reason for what he did…. The closest feeling I can describe to what I felt here was how I felt while reading <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/2761356.The_Sweet_Gum_Tree" title="The Sweet Gum Tree by Katherine Allred" rel="nofollow noopener">The Sweet Gum Tree</a>. In a word: intense and painful.<br><br>But then the reason came out as to why he never showed and it hit me SO hard. Tears were pouring down my face. It was a tragedy of epic proportions. I didn’t think KA would go there, I honestly didn’t, but she did and my heart is still hurting when I think about what happened to him.<br><br>It took Creed and Sylvie up until about the half way mark to sort out their past, but once they did, they became functional to an extreme with an intense chemistry and H.O.T.N.E.S.S. off the freaking charts. I mean SERIOUSLY hot. Think make-up sex, but a million times hotter because its making up for sixteen years of heart ache.<br><br>I loved Sylvie!!! In a word, she was badass! As one of the protection enforcers for Knight’s business, its literally her job to kick ass. She was just totally one of the guys – an Alpha female not to be messed with . She read, acted and talked exactly like one of the KA men – except with a decidedly feminine twist. I love it!! She took care of herself, no one controlled her. In many ways, she was the female version of Creed.<br><br>I loved that they saw eye to eye, stood toe to toe – badass to badass. Sylvie is Creed. Creed is Sylvie. They were born for each other. Made for each other. I loved that even through unthinkable tragedy and years of separation, the love that they’d had since they were children never faded. It was absolutely BEAUTIFUL.<br><br><blockquote> <i> <b> “I loved the man under me in a way that wasn’t just mean to be. It wasn’t a way we were born to be. It was in a way that needed to be.” </b></i>  </blockquote><br><br>Creed melted my heart. I fell really hard for him and just fell deeper and deeper in love as the story went on. He was a tortured badass whose life and heart was tied to Sylvie. When he came back into her life and found out the truth of what had happened to her, it killed me and yet melted my heart how much it hurt him and how strongly he was devoted to working towards replacing her bad memories with good ones, determined to do everything in his power to put their lives back together.<br><br>I’ll say that there was a point where I was pretty furious with him and even to this moment, I still don’t agree with a series of decisions that he made after they were ripped away from each other (you’ll know what I mean when you get to it). Its not even that I can understand what he did, cuz honestly, I can’t. But its ok. I recognize that he’s not perfect and I can accept him as such. The circumstances were horrific, tragic and I’m not going to judge how people react in those situations… it still doesn’t sit fully right with me, but that’s ok. You don’t love someone cuz they are perfect, you love them flaws and all… and I can say that I completely, 100% LOVE Tucker Creed. Flaws and all.<br><br>Their story is told in present day with flash backs to their past filling in the blanks and answering the myriad of questions that their present day story leads to. I loved how we never got the whole thing at once… we got little snippets here and there that piece together their story… it was really powerful and built up from when they were kids to that fateful day when Creed never showed.<br><br>Creed and Sylvie were just two amazingly wonderful people who life had dealt and unthinkably horrific hand of cards. But they were survivors. Reading this story just made me SICK to my stomach, thinking about the lengths that people in this world will go through to steal happiness from others…<br><br>They were strong before, but the joint trauma of having gone through what they were made to go through makes them closer than you can imagine. Its about the point of how when you meet that person that is The One, even if the world comes crashing down, there is nothing that can erase those feelings.<br><br><blockquote> <i> <b> “For over twenty-seven years, every day, every minute, every second, I’ve loved you, Tucker Creed.” </b></i>  </blockquote><br><br>When you have precious in your life and are willing to do anything and everything in your power to fight to keep it but have it wrenched away form you, have to live without it – with the ache of it missing from your life. That’s what makes it so that when it’s back, there is not one minute, not one second, not a breath that isn’t precious, priceless, full.<br><br><blockquote> <i> <b> “You need me. You won’t stay away and you won’t let me go because, baby, you can’t breathe without me.” </b></i>  </blockquote><br><br>I cried a few times throughout this book, but by the end I was crying so hard I could barely see straight. Happy tears of course :) The end killed me in a wonderful way. It was an BEAUTIFUL, PERFECT, GORGEOUS, AMAZING, INCREDIBLE ending… just WOW.<br><br>I’m tempted to give this one 6 stars. It was THAT good.<br><br><blockquote> <i> <b> “You’re my world, Sylvie. Always have been. Always will be.” </b></i>  </blockquote><br><br>Lol, funny side note… my husband heard me crying from the other room and came in and took one look at my face and went “Jeez, baby, you do this for fun?!?” hahahaaa I sorta tried to smile and wailed out a pretty pathetic “yyeeeeeaaaaahhhh”<br><br>Let me just say that there are a lot of incredibly gifted and talented authors out there, and I mean a LOT. But NO one can write badass like KA does. She truly is the reigning queen of badass.<br><br>And speaking of badass, there were some great cameos in this book - namely from Knight and Hawk (yes, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/12299419.Mystery_Man__Dream_Man___1_" title="Mystery Man (Dream Man, #1) by Kristen Ashley" rel="nofollow noopener">Mystery Man</a> Hawk). I really warmed up to Knight in this book. Like REALLY. To the point where I absolutely freaking ADORED him. I loved his relationshipip with Sylvie – how deeply protective he was of her and how much she meant to him. <i> “Bottom of my soul.” </i> *cluthes heart* … I struggled with his book a lot but in this book, I loved seeing how much he had grown, changed, adapted. It was beautiful and heart warming…. and when Hawk (and his gorgeous dimples) make a fantastic, if brief, appearance for the final 90% craziness, I could barely contain my squees <br><br>CREED was just a gorgeous, beautiful, intense read. One of KA’s best. I’m writing this a day after having finished the book and my heart is still full to the brim with my love for Sylvie and Creed. Their story was emotional exhausting and deeply satisfying.<br><br>I started my review with this line, but I want to end it with it as well. I think its one of the most beautiful lines I’ve ever read. If that doesn’t convey the depth of their love, I don’t know what can.<br><br><blockquote> <i> <b> “Born to love you, baby… Die lovin’ you, my Sylvie.” </b></i>  </blockquote><br><br>CASTING: <br><br>This is the guy I'm seeing as CREED! Just scar and bulk him up a bit in your minds.... HAWWWWTT!! <br><br><img width="100%" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1379767070i/253259.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Then this (and the picture at the top of the review) reminded me of a younger Creed &amp; Sylvie at their pier :)<br><br><img width="100%" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380392403i/755400._SY540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>For more of my reviews, visit <a href="http://aestasbookblog.com" rel="nofollow noopener">Aestas Book Blog</a><br><br>And come join the Aestas Book Blog <a href="http://www.facebook.com/pages/Aestas-Book-Blog/332404836826905" rel="nofollow noopener"> Facebook Page</a></span>

Seduction? Not here either. They just went directly for sex and didn't stop doing it till the end XD Sexual tension? Nope, not here either, as I said they just skipped that right for the sex. I get that this was supposed to be erotica, but I've read some erotic novels myself, and some left me hot and bothered (that was the point right?), but only if I could connect myself with them. Sometimes, one touch, one look, a word is enough so you feel the chemistry between the main characters. With 6-7 orgasms you just feel they're exausted <a href="http://s977.photobucket.com/albums/ae254/Black_Morena/Emoticons/?action=view&amp;current=703126.gif" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">

I guess I wanted more angst or something, or just them not being together so soon lol, yeah I'm messed up XD<br><br><br>Sorry KA, I love you and all your books, but I just didn't feel this one like I did with the others <a href="http://s977.photobucket.com/albums/ae254/Black_Morena/Emoticons/?action=view&amp;current=815594.gif" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">

<span id="freeTextContainer3813477836617917037">Probably my favorite in this series. I loved this second chance love story, I loved badass Sylvie and badass Creed, I loved the emotional part and the steamy part. Another great book from KA, which I adored. I swear this woman can't go wrong. Now, I only wait for Nick Sebring's book. Why do I have a feeling he has something up his sleeve?</span>

<div id="review_416356144" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/416356144" />
    <a title="Karla" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3024056-karla"><img alt="Karla" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1324910771p2/3024056.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/416356144?book_show_action=true">Sep 17, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Karla" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Karla" href="/user/show/3024056-karla">Karla</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3024056-karla?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3024056-karla?shelf=strong-willed-heroine">strong-willed-heroine</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3024056-karla?shelf=angst-filled">angst-filled</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3024056-karla?shelf=awesome-alpha">awesome-alpha</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3024056-karla?shelf=heartbreaking">heartbreaking</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3024056-karla?shelf=kick-ass-heroine">kick-ass-heroine</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3024056-karla?shelf=sweet-romance">sweet-romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3024056-karla?shelf=sensual">sensual</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3024056-karla?shelf=sizzling-romance">sizzling-romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3024056-karla?shelf=yummy-men">yummy-men</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer416356144" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17655643535102947985"><b>An exhausting, utterly satisfying read…I LOVED it!!</b> <br/> <br/>To appreciate this book and the full impact of Creed and Sylvie’s story, I strongly suggest you read every word, every sentence, every page, every chapter, beginning to end, before you come to a conclusion on this book. If you don’t like it after that, then so be it. <b>However</b>, I believe you will find the story captivating, charming, heartbreaking, confusing and at times even frustrating. It’s an emotional roller-coaster, but the payoff is a tru</span>
  <span id="freeText17655643535102947985" style="display:none"><b>An exhausting, utterly satisfying read…I LOVED it!!</b> <br> <br>To appreciate this book and the full impact of Creed and Sylvie’s story, I strongly suggest you read every word, every sentence, every page, every chapter, beginning to end, before you come to a conclusion on this book. If you don’t like it after that, then so be it. <b>However</b>, I believe you will find the story captivating, charming, heartbreaking, confusing and at times even frustrating. It’s an emotional roller-coaster, but the payoff is a truly unique and genuine love story. Annoyance towards the characters will arise, you will have questions, and they will be answered…<b>every single one of them!</b> When all is said and done, you will see Sylvie and Creed in a different light. Their love for each other is rooted in deep in their hearts, and this is the story of how that came to be, why it was lost and how it was found once again. <br><br>Creed was an honorable boy, teen, and man! He never wavered in his commitment to Sylvie and he did not leave her, he was forced to make a decision in a no-win situation, he was baited with an incentive, and I use that word loosely, when brutalizing him…<b>did not work!</b> Sylvie, oh poor Sylvie, she thinks she knows, but she doesn’t, the pain of losing him sets in, and then her own personal hell begins. Creed kept his promise, and when others didn’t, Sylvie ultimately paid the cost…they both lost so much, the worst of it being each other. <br><br>No, the book is not perfect and in places it’s lacking, namely some of the sex scenes. They are frequent and felt incomplete at times. Then there are other moments that are raw and passionate, so much so, it’s as if Sylvie and Creed need to crawl inside each other so they will never be separated again! I would not classify Creed as an anti-hero, however I would say he’s an unfinished-hero, his story’s not done. He needs to be the knight in shining armor to the girl who stole his heart so many years ago. Creed needs to knock down the walls that his Sylvie has built around her, be her man, absorb her pain and bring the soft back into her life! <br><br>It’s an exhausting book, and one that requires the reader to put the pieces of the puzzle that is Tucker Creed together. Keep this in mind, the answers are there and they are plausible and will have you, if not loving this man, at least respecting him. He sacrificed so much for the woman he loves, <b>they</b> both lost so much. At the outset Sylvie is harsh, she has every right to be. She swears like a sailor; yes, she drops the f-bomb, a lot, but mostly in her head. Once she understands what Creed went through, were his mind and heart have been for sixteen years, she accepts him back into her life. At that point they don’t let go, nor do they question that a renewed relationship is inevitable…they go with it, because <b>they are meant to be together!</b> <br><br>Kristen Ashley did an amazing job of keeping the reader on edge. The past and present development worked well. It might anger some readers, as the truth behind Creed’s disappearance is told to Sylvie early on, but it’s only revealed in bits and pieces to the reader throughout the book. So, I can understand how some readers might be frustrated with Creed, not knowing what drove and kept him away. Again, I reiterate the answers are there! They might not always be clear and upfront, but it will all make sense in the end.<br><br>In true Kristen Ashley style she give us a story that toys with our feelings, has us loving people we might otherwise hate, and like we’ve come to expect, takes us on an emotional journey like no other. Then she treats us to her trademark epilogue, and all is right once again in our KA world! <br><br>I had a hard time finding a picture of Creed as he would be today, but this is how I would have seen him as a young man.<br><br><b>Sky blue eyes, messy brown hair, rugged face…my 23 year old Tucker Creed</b><br><a href="http://s1130.photobucket.com/albums/m524/kparks823/?action=view&amp;current=hotties-with-blue-eyes-23.jpg" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380391519i/753993._SY540_.jpg" alt="Photobucket" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br><br>Thanks to my sweet friend Kristen for reading this with me. It was a great ride!! <br><br><br></span>
  <a data-text-id="17655643535102947985" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

And of course there's the great KA epilogues that make you smile. <br><br>A word of caution - if cussing offends you then this book isn't for you. The F word thrown around by both the female and male lead. <br><br>Overall, I enjoyed listening to CREED. I'm thinking listening to KA books is the way to go for me. <div id="review_474411760" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/474411760" />
    <a title="Christy" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/11284813-christy"><img alt="Christy" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1594293998p2/11284813.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/474411760?book_show_action=true">Dec 10, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Christy" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Christy" href="/user/show/11284813-christy">Christy</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer474411760" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3165613008148532085"><b>5 Fabulous Creed and Sylvie Stars!!!!!</b><br/><br/><b>
  <i>“Some people get to live life. Some people survive it. We’re survivors. We can carve out our pieces of happy, and, I swear to god, baby, right now, you got my vow, for you and me, the rest of our lives, I’ll bust my ass to carve our piece of happy.”</i>
</b><br/><br/><a href='http://s1279.beta.photobucket.com/user/Christyb23/media/Creed5_zpsf010333d.gif.html' target='_blank' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380400393i/775774.gif' alt=' photo Creed5_zpsf010333d.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><br/>Six year old Sylvie often ran out of her house when the yelling started. Her father and step mother yelled a lot. One night, she ran into eleven year old Tucker Creed. He doesn’t like the yelling either. T</span>
  <span id="freeText3165613008148532085" style="display:none"><b>5 Fabulous Creed and Sylvie Stars!!!!!</b><br><br><b>
  <i>“Some people get to live life. Some people survive it. We’re survivors. We can carve out our pieces of happy, and, I swear to god, baby, right now, you got my vow, for you and me, the rest of our lives, I’ll bust my ass to carve our piece of happy.”</i>
</b><br><br><a href="http://s1279.beta.photobucket.com/user/Christyb23/media/Creed5_zpsf010333d.gif.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380400393i/775774.gif" alt=" photo Creed5_zpsf010333d.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>Six year old Sylvie often ran out of her house when the yelling started. Her father and step mother yelled a lot. One night, she ran into eleven year old Tucker Creed. He doesn’t like the yelling either. This is where their story begins...<br><br><b>
  <i>“Next time you gotta get away, Sylvie, you come to me.” My breathing felt funny. “What?” I whispered. “It gets bad, you gotta get away, you come to me. I’ll take care of you.”<br><br>“I don’t like being alone.” I whispered. “You’re not anymore.” </i>
</b><br><br>Sylvie and Creed are always there for each other. They meet by the lake, by their pier, as regularly as they can, and Sylvie’s birthday is their special day. Creed has gotten Sylvie the same thing for her birthday ever since she has been seven. They are best friends. As they get older, their relationship changes. <br><br><a href="http://s1279.beta.photobucket.com/user/Christyb23/media/Creed2_zps738a7592.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380400393i/775775.jpg" alt=" photo Creed2_zps738a7592.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><b>
  <i>“Your sixteenth birthday. You got the same thing every year for ten years, but you acted every time like I didn’t hand you some shit necklace but the moon. I looked at you and it hit me it was you. It hit me that it could be no one else but you. You were born to be mine and I was born to be yours.”</i>
</b><br><br>She is seventeen, he is twenty two. They are in love, and they have a plan. When Sylvie turns eighteen, they are going to run away together, leave their messed up lives behind and start fresh. Just the two of them. On Sylvie’s birthday, everything is set to go. But Creed never shows. Sylvie’s life takes a terrible turn. Everything changes for the two of them. Sylvie goes sixteen years with out seeing or hearing from Creed. Her life is good now. She has gotten over her past, and she has a couple of close friends that mean the world to her, then he shows up...<br><br><b>Tucker Creed. My first love, my protector, my savior. My betrayer. </b><br><a href="http://s1279.beta.photobucket.com/user/Christyb23/media/98080ff3-2f5c-4c6f-9c23-790d1151e122_zps9c05ca91.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380400393i/775776._SY540_.jpg" alt=" photo 98080ff3-2f5c-4c6f-9c23-790d1151e122_zps9c05ca91.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br><b>“You’ll always be my Sylvie. Yeah?”</b><br><a href="http://s1279.beta.photobucket.com/user/Christyb23/media/Creed6_zps45799825.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380400393i/775777.jpg" alt=" photo Creed6_zps45799825.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>Sylvie is more than a little shocked to see Creed. And even more surprised to find that he is working for her best friend Knight, and is being partnered with her on a case. Knight had no idea that Creed was the one Sylvie had told him about. Sylvie tries to play it off that its no big deal, but Knight sees straight through her. <br><b>
  <i>“Anya left me or I lost her, I’d never get over it so don’t bullshit me.” he shot back. “There’s only one, we both know it, and Tucker Creed was your one. So you aren’t over it. That doesn’t mean you can’t cope. But you won’t cope if you deny that somewhere inside you can’t.”</i>
</b><br>Can I just throw this out there... I was SO HAPPY to see more of Knight :D <br><br>I absolutely LOVED Sylvie! Not your normal heroine, she was a straight up bad ass and I loved it! Not sure how I felt about Creed at first. I was more than a little hurt with how he abandoned Sylvie, but once you got the whole story... WOW. Creed.. what a guy! When I found out the reason he never showed up, I was more than a little shocked, and upset. Once Sylvie found out, she needed a little time, Creed, not so much. <br><b>
  <i>“I need time.” His head jerked then his eyes locked on mine. “Honest to Christ, give you anything. Anything baby. But lost enough time. Can’t give you that. Space, maybe. Time. No.”</i>
</b><br><br>Sylvie tries to convey to Creed she is not the same girl anymore. Her past changed her. Changed everything. He doesn’t care. He loves her and wants to be there for her, make up for all the lost time. <br><b>
  <i> “Not sure where you are but I’ll state clear where I am. I gave you up once. It killed me. It was figuratively but its still killed me. I’m not doin’ that shit again.”<br><br>“Then and now, beautiful, I’ll take you any way you come to me.” His hands in my hair shook my head gently. “Any way. I love this Sylvie. I loved that Sylvie. I just love you, baby.”</i>
</b><br><br>Once they are together, they are together in every way. They had one of those undeniable connections. And some hot chemistry! And a love worth fighting for. <br><br>This is one of those stories that wasn’t easy to read, they both went through some pretty heavy stuff. But it was such a beautiful love story. Beautiful, but also heartbreaking, traumatic, emotional and amazing. I loved the back and forth between Creed and Sylvie’s past and present. It was great to see my Knight and Hawk in this one too! And the ending/epilogue... pure perfection KA style! Loved it! This one wasn’t quite as good as Knight for me, but still a worthy 5 star read! Looking forward to the next one in this series!!! <br><br><b>
  <i>“On a cold night, a long time ago, you put your hands almost exactly where they are right now and , I might have been six years old, but I fell hard. So, yeah. For over twenty-seven years, every day, every minute, every second, I’ve loved you, Tucker Creed.”<br><br>“You’re my world, Sylvie. Always have been. Always will be.”</i>
</b></span>
  <a data-text-id="3165613008148532085" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

Can she overlook Creed's betrayal? Can he get her back after 16 years? Both had torturous pasts, pasts that tore them apart and shredded them to bits... but this is KA and thankfully that answer is YES (this is not even a spoiler so shhhhh).<br><br><blockquote>

<div id="review_1062589200" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1062589200" />
    <a title="Flo" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7643503-flo"><img alt="Flo" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1597575025p2/7643503.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1062589200?book_show_action=true">Sep 23, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Flo" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Flo" href="/user/show/7643503-flo">Flo</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="ebook " href="/book/show/23322235-creed">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7643503-flo?shelf=second-chance">second-chance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7643503-flo?shelf=abuse">abuse</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7643503-flo?shelf=contemporary-romance">contemporary-romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/7643503-flo?shelf=read-in-2014">read-in-2014</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1062589200" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6861353711922541711"><b>4 yummy frozen Snickers STARS</b><br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1414960277i/11710261.png' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>That was beautiful and heartbreaking and kick-ass and scorching hot and naughty and I sure was a bit bored there for a while...<br/><br/><i>Creed</i> is book number two in the <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/series/77851-unfinished-hero' rel='nofollow noopener'>Unfinished Hero Series</a> and also my second <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/2958084.Kristen_Ashley' rel='nofollow noopener'>Kristen Ashley</a> book. I'm hooked. I swear I will read every book this woman wrote so far and will write in the future. I'm so happy in my fangirl world filled with domineering alpha-male book boyfriends.<br/><br/>Ok, let's do this...my review:<br/><br/><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“Born to love you, baby,” he r</i></b></blockquote></span>
  <span id="freeText6861353711922541711" style="display:none"><b>4 yummy frozen Snickers STARS</b><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1414960277i/11710261.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>That was beautiful and heartbreaking and kick-ass and scorching hot and naughty and I sure was a bit bored there for a while...<br><br><i>Creed</i> is book number two in the <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/series/77851-unfinished-hero" rel="nofollow noopener">Unfinished Hero Series</a> and also my second <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/2958084.Kristen_Ashley" rel="nofollow noopener">Kristen Ashley</a> book. I'm hooked. I swear I will read every book this woman wrote so far and will write in the future. I'm so happy in my fangirl world filled with domineering alpha-male book boyfriends.<br><br>Ok, let's do this...my review:<br><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“Born to love you, baby,” he repeated. “Die lovin’ you, my Sylvie.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br>This time around we meet Creed and Sylvie. Now first off I was happy to see we still operate in Knight's world. In fact Sylvie as well as Creed work for Mr. Seberin and that just means we get a little Knight as a cherry on top. I'm totally fine with that...I take as much as I can get.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1407294993ra/10670058.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Twenty-eight years ago a six year old girl named Sylvie stumbled through the forest, trying to escape the drama and yelling at home and she runs straight into the arms of eleven year old Tucker Creed. A chance encounter that leads to a beautiful friendship and love. Both kids have a hard time with their parents, and together they find strength and a home. For eleven years their whole world revolved around each other until one day it is all taken away. Seemingly lost forever.<br><br>Sounds amazing, right? I know I did a lot of happy dancing as well. ;D<br><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“It’s always you and me.” <br>I nodded again and felt my lips quivering. <br>He kept whispering, “Always me and my Sylvie, yeah?”<br>“Yeah,” I whispered.” </i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br>Sixteen years later <b>Sylvie Bissenette</b> is one kick-ass woman. She is working as a PI and on the side she does a little work for Knight. (Not going to tell you exactly what in case you haven't read the first book.) She is independent, strong and it is apparent that there are some ghosts in her past. One of those ghosts re-emerges one morning in her bedroom and she greats him with a gun to his head. <br><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“He crossed his arms again and requested, “You wanna stop aiming your weapon at me?”<br>Actually, no. I didn’t. I wanted to keep aiming my gun at him and I might also want to pull the trigger.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br>Sylvie hasn't seen Creed since her eighteenth birthday and finding him standing at the bottom of her bed is not what she expected to happen. He had abandoned her, left her to suffer a nightmare and now he is back looking all hot and yummy like...and claims to be her new partner. Not fair!<br><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“Some people get to live life. Some people survive it. We’re survivors. We can carve out our piece of happy, and, I swear to God, baby, right now, you got my vow, for you and for me, the rest of our lives, I’ll bust my ass to carve our piece of happy.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br><b>Tucker Creed</b> is one hell of a man and he was one hell of a boy when he knew Sylvie, but a lot of time has passed and the last sixteen years haven't been easy on him either. The best day he had in years was when Knight hired him as an outside source (yes, they work in the same field) to find a leak in his operation and Creed discovered the identity of his new partner. And now his single most important goal in life is to get her back and get his life back. <br><br>The story is told from Sylvie's POV and for a while we don't really know if Creed is a good guy and what exactly happened to make him leave. Each book of the <i>Unfinished Hero</i> series is based on another guy, but in the beginning Sylvie was the stronger and more dominant (and I don't mean that in a sexual way) character. I even read that KA considered naming the book Sylvie, but Creed pulled through and he blossomed into a wonderful character; who is not only equal to Sylvie in charisma and gravitas, but also managed to be one hell of a book boyfriend. <br><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“Then and now, beautiful, I’ll take you any way you come to me … Any way. I love this Sylvie, I loved that Sylvie. I just love you, baby.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br>Yes, Mr. Creed is a hard ass, who knows what he wants, who is control and basically rocks your freaking socks off, but at the same time he is a sweet and caring man, who despite the hardship and loss that life has given him carries on and doesn't crack under the pressure.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1405779511ra/10450418.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Sylvie and Creed's story is quite wonderful. They have a lot of obstacles to overcome and things to deal with that are not easy, but they try their best. They are both such strong human beings and oh boy, do they clash and bicker and fight and they make up... And they do so mainly in a horizontal dance. *fans self* HAWT and even a little kinky!!!<br><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“I’m not what you want, Sylvie, I get that because it’s the same for you as it is for me. I’m not what you want ’cause I’m what you need.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br>I loved how KA pulled this whole story together by basing Sylvie and Creed in the future, while giving flashbacks into their past - how they met and how they got to the point where they didn't even know the other person was still alive. <br><br>After reading <i>Knight</i> I am aware that KA has a certain very elaborate style to write a book and she is detail oriented, but this time around I have to critique the middle part. It is simply too long for hardly any major plot developments. I do realise that the protagonists have to find and get to know each other again, but some parts felt repetitive and overdrawn. Also, the reason Creed was hired and the whole plot line that came with it was underwhelming to say the least. She really could have used that one a little better.<br><br>In all fairness, the ending made up for it. There is some major ass kicking involved as well as some cheesy goodness. All in all a heartbreaking and beautiful story...definitely worth a read and I'm on to the next one...<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1384582622ra/6907180.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1418911509i/12944326.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><a href="http://coffeeaddictbooks.blogspot.co.at/" rel="nofollow noopener">

<div id="review_339823478" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/339823478" />
    <a title="~ Becs ~" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2626261-becs"><img alt="~ Becs ~" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1388693144p2/2626261.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/339823478?book_show_action=true">May 30, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="~ Becs ~" class="user" itemprop="url" name="~ Becs ~" href="/user/show/2626261-becs">~ Becs ~</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2626261-becs?shelf=abused-heroine">abused-heroine</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2626261-becs?shelf=alpha-hero">alpha-hero</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2626261-becs?shelf=lost-love-rekindled">lost-love-rekindled</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2626261-becs?shelf=tortured-abused-hero">tortured-abused-hero</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2626261-becs?shelf=tattooed-hero">tattooed-hero</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2626261-becs?shelf=contemporary-romance">contemporary-romance</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer339823478" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6227652147505921127">Well, I’m finding this one really hard to review. <br/><br/>Sylvie and Creed, both victims of bad parenting and awful childhoods, were about to run away together when she turned 18 when her father managed to separate them in the cruellest way. Sylvie now works for Knight Sebring and Creed is brought in on the case and they are thrown together and have to deal with their past. So the story is told in the now and in the past as we get Sylvie and Creed now and then.<br/><br/>I have to say that I didn’t totally love th</span>
  <span id="freeText6227652147505921127" style="display:none">Well, I’m finding this one really hard to review. <br /><br />Sylvie and Creed, both victims of bad parenting and awful childhoods, were about to run away together when she turned 18 when her father managed to separate them in the cruellest way. Sylvie now works for Knight Sebring and Creed is brought in on the case and they are thrown together and have to deal with their past. So the story is told in the now and in the past as we get Sylvie and Creed now and then.<br /><br />I have to say that I didn’t totally love this. Creed is very much a typical KA uber-alpa hero – he talks the talk and behaves pretty much as all her other heroes. Sylvie is a little different from the regular KA heroine – in fact; she’s much more like one of her heroes.<br /><br />The story is entirely Sylvie and Creed. There’s not really much else going on. They are working a case for Knight trying to find a mole in his operation but this plot line never really revs up and is resolved fairly quickly and quietly. I did love the first half of the book, the revelations and Sylvie and Creed’s rekindling of their relationship but this is completely finished by the 50% mark and then nothing else happens. It became repetitive with Creed and Sylvie saying the same things over and over and having sex and her getting to know his kids. You could probably have skipped the second half of the book entirely and not miss anything.<br /><br />Also, I really didn’t connect with the characters. Usually KA’s heroes and heroines spring vividly to life in my imagination and totally exist there but these two really just felt like words on a page. At first, I found Sylvie refreshingly different but, mostly, I couldn’t empathise with her. She and Creed just didn’t seem very real to me. I also didn’t find it very sexy. It’s definitely not erotica, it’s fairly steamy contemporary romance but I didn’t find it very hot – the sex was repetitive and definitely not kinky.<br /><br />This series is supposed to be ‘unfinished heroes’, maybe anti-heroes but Creed is just a straight up hero. He’s one of the good guys – his only crime is to be hired by Knight. Other than that, he doesn’t fit the bill. <br /><br />I can’t quite work out why this one didn’t work for me – maybe it’s been too much of a good thing as it’s really not very different from any of her other books and I’m really quite sad not to love this even though I very much enjoyed the first half of the book.<br /><br />3 stars for the first half of the book.<br /><br />For more of my reviews, please visit my <a href="http://sinfullysexybooks.blogspot.co.uk/" rel="nofollow noopener">Sinfully Sexy Book Blog</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="6227652147505921127" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer337112980" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer17390280742786813337"><b> Creed & Sylvie.. Just hot</b><br/><br/>Once again Ms. Ashley brought it home with the 2nd installment to this series. To say that we KA fans & fans of this series were losing our minds waiting for this book, would be an understatement. I mean we were all literally STALKING the internet waiting for this book to be released.<br/><br/>Yes this was us..<br/><a href='http://s1135.photobucket.com/albums/m630/Enhya77/?action=view&current=tumblr_lcol89XzFJ1qb6zck.gif' target='_blank' rel='nofollow noopener'>

</a><br/>LOL so you get the idea.<br/><br/>It was certainly well worth the wait I must say. I truly enjoyed this one and could not be moved from</span>
  <span id="freeText17390280742786813337" style="display:none"><b> Creed &amp; Sylvie.. Just hot</b><br><br>Once again Ms. Ashley brought it home with the 2nd installment to this series. To say that we KA fans &amp; fans of this series were losing our minds waiting for this book, would be an understatement. I mean we were all literally STALKING the internet waiting for this book to be released.<br><br>Yes this was us..<br><a href="http://s1135.photobucket.com/albums/m630/Enhya77/?action=view&amp;current=tumblr_lcol89XzFJ1qb6zck.gif" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380222758ra/358661.gif" alt="Photobucket" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><a href="http://s1135.photobucket.com/albums/m630/Enhya77/?action=view&amp;current=tumblr_m2urwthZmw1r99v5f.gif" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380222758ra/421922.gif" alt="Photobucket" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>And when we finally got our Creed..<br><a href="http://s1135.photobucket.com/albums/m630/Enhya77/?action=view&amp;current=tumblr_m91fbtZ36j1qhjw1v.gif" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380222758ra/368577.gif" alt="Photobucket" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br>LOL so you get the idea.<br><br>It was certainly well worth the wait I must say. I truly enjoyed this one and could not be moved from my laptop.<br><br>It took me a bit, but not too long to really become enthralled with this story, though I was not sure how I was feeling about Sylvie. I like her. She's a strong cookie, but I wasn't sure how I was feeling overall about her purpose or place within this story. And Creed, I was blown away and conflicted and eager to know why he and Sylvie suffered and was ultimately torn apart for so many years. Once I admitted my eargerness to know the deal, shortly it was revealed &amp; thus began my sobbing, screaming, laughing, heart pumping into my throat reactions, concerning this book.<br><br>I was suprised that we got to see alot more of Knight in this one than I thought we would. And there were a few heartfelt, heartwarming just OMG! scenes involving he and Sylvie. I loved this. And I loved Anya in this as well. But ultimately Knight will always just leave me beside myself..<br><br>The reason why this one gets 4 instead of 5 stars from me is because I felt the issues that brought Sylvie &amp; Creed's story to the forefront in the first place (their jobs) was glossed over and ended very anti-climactic to me.<br><br>Which was a bummer for me cos this is what dominated the story for the 1st 11 or so chapters. And Knight's brother Nick??? WTHeck happened there? And Why? And of course the build up to what led to Creed being Sylvie's first was great, but when it actually happened I was like "Really? That's it?" Yeah, that left me wanting big time.<br><br><br>So there were things in this one that I felt needed to be a bit tighter within the story to give a little more balanced feel to it.<br><br>But I do love their story. It was beautiful, it was frightening at times. Heartbreaking. But over all just a beautiful, spiritual journey. And I loved it. The growth that you see happening with Sylvie as an individual and a woman in love, was done superbly I think. And the responsibility you see on Creed's shoulders, how he handles and tackles their demons and not just on his own, I thought shown through beautifully. Another great installment.<br><br>So.. READ IT!!<br>I HIGHLY recommend this read.</span>

<div id="review_334191185" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/334191185" />
    <a title="Shawna" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1802746-shawna"><img alt="Shawna" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1574172018p2/1802746.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/334191185?book_show_action=true">May 21, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Shawna" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Shawna" href="/user/show/1802746-shawna">Shawna</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">KA addicts &amp; fans of steamy contemporary romance</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1802746-shawna?shelf=contemporary-romance">contemporary-romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1802746-shawna?shelf=hero-commoner-self-made">hero-commoner-self-made</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1802746-shawna?shelf=romance-doesnt-end-at-40">romance-doesnt-end-at-40</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1802746-shawna?shelf=format-ebook">format-ebook</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1802746-shawna?shelf=hero-nice-guy-gets-the-girl">hero-nice-guy-gets-the-girl</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1802746-shawna?shelf=erotic-romance-erotica-romantica">erotic-romance-erotica-romantica</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1802746-shawna?shelf=hh-social-class-wealth-matters">hh-social-class-wealth-matters</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1802746-shawna?shelf=friends-to-lovers">friends-to-lovers</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1802746-shawna?shelf=favorite-romance-series">favorite-romance-series</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1802746-shawna?shelf=hero-tattalizing">hero-tattalizing</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer334191185" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2195456966091713463">5 stars – Contemporary Erotic Romance<br/><br/>Kristen Ashley has without a doubt earned the best/most of everything for 2012 (addictive stories, unforgettable heroes, and moving epilogues) and is easily one of my all-time favorite authors. Her books completely beguile me every single time and this was certainly no exception. Never mind that I had boxes to unpack or a gazillion other things to do because <b>Creed</b> simply demanded my full attention...and boy howdy, he got it! I simply couldn’t put it down!<br/><br/>This</span>
  <span id="freeText2195456966091713463" style="display:none">5 stars – Contemporary Erotic Romance<br /><br />Kristen Ashley has without a doubt earned the best/most of everything for 2012 (addictive stories, unforgettable heroes, and moving epilogues) and is easily one of my all-time favorite authors. Her books completely beguile me every single time and this was certainly no exception. Never mind that I had boxes to unpack or a gazillion other things to do because <b>Creed</b> simply demanded my full attention...and boy howdy, he got it! I simply couldn’t put it down!<br /><br />This actually started off a little bit rocky and I wasn’t quite sure what to think. But then around the 28% mark, everything started falling into place and I ended up loving it! Creed and Sylvie are both broken and battered with horribly tragic pasts, but they find healing and forgiveness through their resilient, enduring, and unconquerable love for each other. They’re memorable, unique characters, and I adored them together. <br /><br />I loved <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/13565914.Knight__Unfinished_Hero___1_" title="Knight (Unfinished Hero, #1) by Kristen Ashley" rel="nofollow noopener">Knight</a> and <b>Creed</b>, and it’s hard to decide which I liked better. Both have compelling, strong, albeit very distinctive, heroes, and although related, they’re still very different books; so it’s probably best not to compare the two. Having said that, this definitely left me more emotionally satisfied than <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/13565914.Knight__Unfinished_Hero___1_" title="Knight (Unfinished Hero, #1) by Kristen Ashley" rel="nofollow noopener">Knight</a>, probably because there’s a definitive, more traditional, hard-won HEA. <br /><br />Bottom line, Kristen Ashley is an author goddess and she’s once again made me a very happy romance reader! Big 5 stars!<br /><br /><u>Most sigh-worthy moments</u>:<br /> <br />Creed’s back tattoo...just <i>faint</i>.<br /><br />The necklaces...just <i>swoon</i>.<br /><br />The <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[proposal scene with roses on the bed <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>...so <i>awww romantic</i>.<br /><br />The epilogue...of course. KA is the queen of heartwarming, mushy, gushy, and can’t-get-enough-of-it epilogues, and <b>Creed</b> left me smiling and wiping away tears. <br /><br /><u>Minor criticisms</u>: <br /><br />Creed naming his kids <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[with another woman the same names that he and Sylvie had planned on <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> made my heart break. Talk about a hot poker to the chest! His reasoning was awful, twisted, beautiful, and tragic, and although things eventually worked out, it was still hard to take. <br /> <br />After waiting so long for the flashback scene to reveal the moment that Sylvie <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[finally lost her virginity to Creed <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>, I was very disappointed that it faded to black.<br /><br />I think it’s a bit misleading that this series falls in the <i>Unfinished Hero</i> series that’s described as erotic romances with anti-heroes because Creed is without a doubt an honorable man and a full-fledged hero, and it’s really not all that erotic.<br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="2195456966091713463" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>
